This skill bridges the gap by analyzing a workflow and generating a new CLI module that uses these proven patterns.\n    28â†’\n    29â†’## What Gets Generated\n    30â†’\n    31â†’A CLI subcommand package under `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`:\n    32â†’\n    33â†’| File | Purpose | When Generated |\n    34â†’|------|---------|----------------|\n    35â†’| `models.py` | Domain types extending `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult` | Always |\n    36â†’| `gates.py` | `GateCriteria` + semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]` | Always |\n    37â†’| `prompts.py` | LLM contract builders per Claude-assisted step | Always |\n    38â†’| `config.py` | CLI arg resolution, file discovery, config construction | Always |\n    39â†’| `executor.py` | Synchronous supervisor loop with `ThreadPoolExecutor` for parallelism | Always |\n    40â†’| `monitor.py` | NDJSON incremental output parser with domain signals | Always |\n    41â†’| `process.py` | `ClaudeProcess` subclass with domain-specific prompt building | Always |\n    42â†’| `tui.py` | Rich live dashboard with gate state machine | Always |\n    43â†’| `logging_.py` | Dual JSONL + Markdown execution logging | Always |\n    44â†’| `diagnostics.py` | `DiagnosticCollector`, `FailureClassifier`, `ReportGenerator` | Always |\n    45â†’| `commands.py` | Click CLI group and subcommands | Always |\n    46â†’| `__init__.py` | Package exports | Always |\n    47â†’| `inventory.py` | Pure-programmatic file discovery/classification | If workflow has discovery steps |\n    48â†’| `filtering.py` | Pure-programmatic inter-step data filtering | If workflow has filtering between steps |\n    49â†’\n    50â†’These file definitions inform the pipeline specification produced in Phase 2.\n    51â†’\n    52â†’## Required Input\n    53â†’\n    54â†’```\n    55â†’/sc:cli-portify --workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>]\n    56â†’```\n    57â†’\n    58â†’| Argument | Required | Description |\n    59â†’|----------|----------|-------------|\n    60â†’| `--workflow` | Yes | Skill directory path or `sc-*` name to portify |\n    61â†’| `--name` | No | CLI subcommand name (default: derived from workflow) |\n    62â†’| `--output` | No | Output directory (default: `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`) |\n    63â†’| `--dry-run` | No | Show decomposition plan without generating spec |\n    64â†’\n    65â†’**STOP** if `--workflow` is not provided or the path doesn't resolve to a valid skill.\n    66â†’\n    67â†’## Behavioral Flow\n    68â†’\n    69â†’Four phases, each producing artifacts that feed the next. Present output to user for review after Phases 1 and 2 before continuing.\n    70â†’\n    71â†’### Phase 1: Workflow Analysis\n    72â†’\n    73â†’Load `refs/analysis-protocol.md` before this phase. It contains the discovery checklist, step decomposition algorithm, classification rubric, and output format template.\n    74â†’\n    75â†’**Goal**: Decompose the target workflow into a structured pipeline specification.\n    76â†’\n    77â†’1. **Discover components** â€” Find the command `.md`, skill `SKILL.md`, all `refs/` and `rules/`, all `templates/`, all `scripts/`, and all referenced agents. Build a component inventory table with paths, line counts, and purposes.\n    78â†’\n    79â†’2. **Map the protocol** â€” Extract the step-by-step behavioral flow. Pay attention to:\n    80â†’   - Wave/phase boundaries in the skill\n    81â†’   - Agent delegation patterns (which agent, parallel vs sequential)\n    82â†’   - Conditional execution paths (flags that skip steps)\n    83â†’   - Implicit inter-step data flow (what one step produces that another consumes)\n    84â†’\n    85â†’3. **Identify steps** â€” A new Step boundary exists when:\n    86â†’   - A new artifact is produced\n    87â†’   - A different agent takes over\n    88â†’   - Execution mode changes (sequential â†’ parallel)\n    89â†’   - A quality gate must be evaluated\n    90â†’   - Operation type changes (analysis â†’ generation â†’ validation)\n    91â†’\n    92â†’4. **Classify each step** on the programmatic spectrum:\n    93â†’   - **Pure programmatic**: Runs as a Python function, no Claude subprocess. Examples: file inventory via `git ls-files`, config construction, file filtering between passes, scoring formulas, structural validation, batch assignment. If the logic is deterministic and the input/output formats are well-defined, it should be programmatic.\n    94â†’   - **Claude-assisted**: Runs as a Claude subprocess with a prompt contract and gate. Examples: content analysis, writing reports, rubric-based assessment, creative synthesis, debate.\n    95â†’   - **Hybrid**: Programmatic setup â†’ Claude subprocess â†’ programmatic validation. Examples: steps that need Claude for content but have strict structural validation on the output.\n    96â†’\n    97â†’5. **Map dependencies and parallel groups** â€” Draw the data flow: which steps produce artifacts consumed by downstream steps? Which steps are independent and can run concurrently? For batched workflows, identify where batch parallelism applies.\n    98â†’\n    99â†’6. **Extract gates** â€” For each step output, identify what validation the original workflow expects. Map these to gate tiers: EXEMPT (informational), LIGHT (exists + non-empty), STANDARD (structural checks), STRICT (structural + semantic).\n   100â†’\n   101â†’7. **Assign gate modes** â€” `GateMode.BLOCKING` for steps whose output feeds downstream steps. `GateMode.TRAILING` for quality-only checks that don't affect data flow.\n   102â†’\n   103â†’**Output**: `portify-analysis.md` â€” Complete decomposition following the template in `refs/analysis-protocol.md`. Must include: component inventory, step graph with classifications, parallel groups, gates summary, data flow diagram, and recommendations.\n   104â†’\n   105â†’**Present to user for review before Phase 2.**\n   106â†’\n   107â†’### Phase 2: Pipeline Specification\n   108â†’\n   109â†’Load `refs/pipeline-spec.md` before this phase. It contains Step definition patterns, model design patterns, gate patterns, executor patterns, and the new unified-audit-gating patterns (TurnLedger, gate modes, subprocess isolation, context injection, resume semantics).\n   110â†’\n   111â†’**Goal**: Convert the analysis into concrete, code-ready specifications.\n   112â†’\n   113â†’1. **Design the Step graph** â€” Map each workflow step to `Step` objects. Batched parallel steps are `list[Step]` groups. Dynamic step counts (e.g., batch count determined at runtime) require a `build_steps()` function.\n   114â†’\n   115â†’2. **Define models** â€” Design domain-specific dataclasses:\n   116â†’   - Config extending `PipelineConfig` with workflow-specific fields (source paths, pass selection, batch sizes, stall/timeout policies)\n   117â†’   - Status enum with domain-specific states (e.g., `VALIDATION_FAIL`, `CRITICAL_FAIL` for audit workflows)\n   118â†’   - Result extending `StepResult` with execution telemetry\n   119â†’   - Aggregate result with `resume_command()` and `suggested_resume_budget`\n   120â†’   - Monitor state with domain-specific NDJSON signals\n   121â†’   - `TurnLedger` integration for budget tracking\n   122â†’\n   123â†’3. **Design prompts** â€” For each Claude-assisted step, write the prompt builder. Each prompt must specify:\n   124â†’   - What input files/context to embed (inline for <50KB, `--file` args for larger)\n   125â†’   - Required output sections and frontmatter fields\n   126â†’   - Machine-readable markers: `EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE|HALT`\n   127â†’   - Any structural requirements the gate will check\n   128â†’\n   129â†’   If prompts collectively exceed ~300 lines, put them in a separate `portify-prompts.md`.\n   130â†’\n   131â†’4. **Design gates** â€” For each output artifact, define:\n   132â†’   - `GateCriteria` with tier, required frontmatter, min lines, semantic checks\n   133â†’   - `GateMode` (BLOCKING or TRAILING)\n   134â†’   - All semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]`\n   135â†’\n   136â†’5. **Implement pure-programmatic steps** â€” Write actual runnable Python code for steps classified as \"pure programmatic\". These run as direct function calls in the executor, bypassing `ClaudeProcess`. Include: file discovery, domain classification, batch assignment, inter-pass filtering, config construction.\n   137â†’\n   138â†’6. **Design the executor** â€” Sprint-style synchronous supervisor:\n   139â†’   - `ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism (NOT async/await)\n   140â†’   - `time.sleep()` polling loops for monitoring\n   141â†’   - Per-step/batch monitoring with stall detection\n   142â†’   - `TurnLedger` budget guards before each launch\n   143â†’   - Runner-authored truth: reports from observed data, not Claude self-reporting\n   144â†’   - Subprocess isolation (4-layer model) for child Claude sessions\n   145â†’   - Context injection: prior results compressed into subsequent prompts\n   146â†’   - Signal-aware shutdown with `SignalHandler`\n   147â†’\n   148â†’7. **Plan integration** â€” Click command group, main.py import, file generation order.\n   149â†’\n   150â†’**Output**: `portify-spec.md` (+ optional `portify-prompts.md`) â€” Complete code spec with models, gates, executor design, pure-programmatic implementations, and integration plan.\n   151â†’\n   152â†’**Present to user for approval before Phase 3.**\n   153â†’\n   154â†’### Phase 3: Release Spec Synthesis\n   155â†’\n   156â†’**Phase 2â†’3 Entry Gate**: Before beginning Phase 3, verify ALL of the following:\n   157â†’- Phase 2 contract `status: completed`\n   158â†’- All blocking checks passed (no unresolved BLOCKING gate failures)\n   159â†’- Phase 2 `step_mapping` contains â‰Ą1 entry\n   160â†’\n   161â†’**STOP** if any entry gate condition fails. Report which condition failed and emit the return contract with `failure_phase: 3, failure_type: prerequisite_failed`.\n   162â†’\n   163â†’**Goal**: Generate a complete, reviewed release specification from Phase 1 and Phase 2 outputs. Record the wall clock start time for `phase_3_seconds` timing instrumentation.\n   164â†’\n   165â†’**Timing**: Record `phase_3_start = current_time()` at the beginning of this phase. NFR-001 advisory target: Phase 3 should complete within 10 minutes wall clock (non-blocking; exceeding this target emits a warning but does not halt the pipeline).\n   166â†’\n   167â†’#### Step 3a: Template Instantiation\n   168â†’\n   169â†’1. Load the release spec template from `src/superclaude/examples/release-spec-template.md`\n   170â†’2. Create a working copy at `{work_dir}/portify-release-spec.md`\n   171â†’3. Verify the working copy was created successfully and contains the template content\n   172â†’\n   173â†’#### Step 3b: Content Population\n   174â†’\n   175â†’Fill template sections from Phase 1 (workflow analysis) and Phase 2 (pipeline specification) outputs using the following mapping table. For each template section, replace `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` sentinels with content derived from the specified source:\n   176â†’\n   177â†’| # | Template Section | Source |\n   178â†’|---|-----------------|--------|\n   179â†’| 1 | Problem Statement | Derive from source workflow's purpose + why portification is needed |\n   180â†’| 2 | Solution Overview | Phase 2 pipeline architecture (step graph, executor design) |\n   181â†’| 2.2 | Workflow / Data Flow | Phase 1 data flow diagram, adapted for the target pipeline |\n   182â†’| 3 | Functional Requirements | One FR per generated pipeline step from Phase 2 `step_mapping` â€” every `step_mapping` entry MUST produce a corresponding FR (SC-004) |\n   183â†’| 4 | Architecture | Phase 2 `module_plan` (new files), Phase 0 prerequisites (modified files) |\n   184â†’| 4.5 | Data Models | Phase 2 model designs (Config, Status, Result, MonitorState) |\n   185â†’| 4.6 | Implementation Order | Phase 2 module dependency order |\n   186â†’| 5.2 | Gate Criteria | Phase 2 `gate_definitions` |\n   187â†’| 5.3 | Phase Contracts | Phase 1+2 contract schemas |\n   188â†’| 6 | NFRs | Standard portification NFRs (sync execution, gate signatures, runner-authored truth) |\n   189â†’| 7 | Risk Assessment | Derived from Phase 1 classification confidence scores + unsupported patterns |\n   190â†’| 8 | Test Plan | Structural test plan from Phase 2 pattern coverage matrix |\n   191â†’| 10 | Downstream Inputs | Themes for sc:roadmap, tasks for sc:tasklist |\n   192â†’\n   193â†’After populating all sections, run SC-003 self-validation: verify zero remaining `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` sentinels in the working copy. If any remain, resolve them before proceeding.\n   194â†’\n   195â†’#### Step 3c: Automated Brainstorm Pass\n   196â†’\n   197â†’Apply embedded brainstorm behavioral patterns as a non-interactive automated pass against the draft spec. This is NOT an invocation of the `sc:brainstorm` command (which is interactive/Socratic); instead, cycle through each of three personas to analyze the draft spec for gaps:\n   198â†’\n   199â†’**Persona perspectives** (apply each in sequence):\n   200â†’\n   201â†’1. **Architect persona**: Analyze for structural gaps â€” missing dependencies, incomplete module boundaries, scaling concerns, cross-module interaction gaps, missing error handling paths\n   202â†’2. **Analyzer persona**: Analyze for logical gaps â€” uncovered edge cases, ambiguous requirements, missing acceptance criteria, inconsistent cross-references, untestable requirements\n   203â†’3. **Backend persona**: Analyze for implementation gaps â€” missing data models, incomplete API contracts, undefined error states, missing retry/timeout specifications, resource lifecycle gaps\n   204â†’\n   205â†’**Structured output format**: Each finding uses the schema:\n   206â†’```\n   207â†’{gap_id, description, severity(high|medium|low), affected_section, persona}\n   208â†’```\n   209â†’\n   210â†’Example:\n   211â†’```\n   212â†’{GAP-001, \"No retry policy defined for failed gate checks\", medium, \"5.2 Gate Criteria\", architect}\n   213â†’```\n   214â†’\n   215â†’**Zero-gap handling**: If no gaps are identified across all three personas, produce an explicit summary:\n   216â†’> \"No gaps identified by architect, analyzer, and backend personas. Spec coverage assessed as complete.\"\n   217â†’\n   218â†’Set `gaps_identified: 0` in the return contract. Zero gaps is a valid outcome â€” it does not block the pipeline.\n   219â†’\n   220â†’**Output**: Append a `## Brainstorm Gap Analysis` section (Section 12) to the draft spec containing all findings in the structured format, or the zero-gap summary.\n   221â†’\n   222â†’#### Step 3d: Gap Incorporation\n   223â†’\n   224â†’Review each brainstorm finding and route it:\n   225â†’\n   226â†’- **Actionable findings** (findings that can be directly addressed): Incorporate into the relevant spec body section identified by `affected_section`. Mark the finding as `[INCORPORATED]` in the gap analysis table.\n   227â†’- **Unresolvable items** (findings that require external input, are out of scope, or cannot be resolved within the spec): Route to Section 11 (Open Items) with the gap ID, question, impact, and resolution target. Mark the finding as `[OPEN]` in the gap analysis table.\n   228â†’\n   229â†’After incorporation, update the gap analysis summary with counts: `{total_gaps, incorporated, open, severity_distribution}`.\n   230â†’\n   231â†’**Timing**: Record `phase_3_end = current_time()`. Compute `phase_3_seconds = phase_3_end - phase_3_start`. Populate `phase_timing.phase_3_seconds` in the return contract. If `phase_3_seconds > 600`, emit warning: \"Phase 3 exceeded 10-minute advisory target (NFR-001)\".\n   232â†’\n   233â†’**Output**: `{work_dir}/portify-release-spec.md` â€” Complete draft spec with brainstorm gap analysis section and incorporated findings.\n   234â†’\n   235â†’**Phase 3â†’4 automatic gate**: Draft spec populated (no `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` values remain) AND brainstorm section (Section 12) present in draft spec.\n   236â†’\n   237â†’### Phase 4: Spec Panel Review\n   238â†’\n   239â†’Embed `sc:spec-panel` behavioral patterns in a convergent review loop. Like Phase 3's brainstorm, this embeds spec-panel behavioral patterns directly rather than invoking the `sc:spec-panel` command (Constraint 1: no inter-skill command invocation).\n   240â†’\n   241â†’**Timing**: Record `phase_4_start = current_time()` at the beginning of this phase. NFR-002 advisory target: Phase 4 should complete within 15 minutes wall clock (non-blocking; exceeding this target emits a warning but does not halt the pipeline).\n   242â†’\n   243â†’#### Step 4a: Focus Pass\n   244â†’\n   245â†’Apply spec-panel behavioral patterns with `--focus correctness,architecture` against `portify-release-spec.md`. This pass embeds four expert analysis patterns inline:\n   246â†’\n   247â†’**Expert analysis patterns** (apply each in sequence, building on prior context):\n   248â†’\n   249â†’1. **Fowler (Architecture)**: Analyze interface design quality, bounded context boundaries, module coupling/cohesion, dependency direction, and design pattern appropriateness. Annotate data flows with count divergence analysis â€” for each transformation, document input count, output count, and whether the spec accounts for count differences.\n   250â†’\n   251â†’2. **Nygard (Reliability/Failure Modes)**: Analyze failure mode coverage, circuit breaker patterns, timeout specifications, retry policies, and recovery mechanisms. Extend guard boundary analysis to include zero/empty cases â€” for every guard condition, verify the spec defines behavior for zero, empty, null, and negative inputs.\n   252â†’\n   253â†’3. **Whittaker (Adversarial)**: Apply five attack methodologies (Zero/Empty, Divergence, Sentinel Collision, Sequence, Accumulation) against each identified invariant. Produce concrete attack scenarios with state traces demonstrating specification gaps.\n   254â†’\n   255â†’4. **Crispin (Testing)**: Analyze testing strategy coverage, acceptance criteria quality, edge case identification, and quality attribute specifications. Generate boundary value test cases for every guard condition and state variable covering: below minimum, at minimum, typical, at maximum, above maximum, and degenerate (zero/empty/null).\n   256â†’\n   257â†’**Focus dimensions**: `correctness` and `architecture` â€” findings must address both dimensions (SC-006).\n   258â†’\n   259â†’**Output format**: Each finding uses the structured schema:\n   260â†’```\n   261â†’{finding_id, severity(CRITICAL|MAJOR|MINOR), expert, location, issue, recommendation}\n   262â†’```\n   263â†’\n   264â†’Where:\n   265â†’- `finding_id`: Unique identifier (e.g., `F-001`, `F-002`)\n   266â†’- `severity`: One of `CRITICAL` (spec provably wrong), `MAJOR` (spec ambiguous/incomplete), `MINOR` (spec could be clearer)\n   267â†’- `expert`: One of `Fowler`, `Nygard`, `Whittaker`, `Crispin`\n   268â†’- `location`: Section/requirement reference in the spec\n   269â†’- `issue`: Description of the identified problem\n   270â†’- `recommendation`: Specific actionable fix\n   271â†’\n   272â†’Additionally produce, if applicable:\n   273â†’- Guard Condition Boundary Table (Nygard leads, Crispin validates, Whittaker attacks)\n   274â†’- Pipeline Quantity Flow Diagram (Fowler leads, if pipeline stages detected)\n   275â†’- State Variable Registry (if 3+ mutable state variables identified)\n   276â†’\n   277â†’#### Step 4b: Focus Incorporation\n   278â†’\n   279â†’Review focus findings from step 4a. Route each finding by severity level. All modifications MUST be additive-only â€” append or extend spec sections only, do not rewrite existing content (Constraint 2, NFR-008).\n   280â†’\n   281â†’**Severity routing**:\n   282â†’\n   283â†’- **CRITICAL findings**: MUST be addressed. Either:\n   284â†’  - Incorporate the fix into the relevant spec body section identified by `location`, OR\n   285â†’  - Document a written justification for dismissal in the panel report (Constraint 7). Dismissal justification must include: `finding_id`, reason for dismissal, and assessment of downstream impact.\n   286â†’- **MAJOR findings**: Incorporate into the corresponding spec body section identified by `location`. Modifications use append/extend only.\n   287â†’- **MINOR findings**: Append to Section 11 (Open Items) with the `finding_id`, issue summary, and recommended resolution target.\n   288â†’\n   289â†’All modifications are traceable by `finding_id` from step 4a output. Mark each finding as `[INCORPORATED]`, `[DISMISSED]`, or `[OPEN]` in the focus findings table.\n   290â†’\n   291â†’#### Step 4c: Critique Pass\n   292â†’\n   293â†’Apply spec-panel behavioral patterns with `--mode critique` against the updated spec (after step 4b incorporation). Run the full expert panel in critique review sequence:\n   294â†’\n   295â†’1. Fowler â€” Architecture and interface design\n   296â†’2. Nygard â€” Reliability and failure mode analysis\n   297â†’3. Whittaker â€” Adversarial attack-based specification probing\n   298â†’4. Crispin â€” Testing strategy and acceptance criteria\n   299â†’\n   300â†’Each expert produces quality dimension scores and prioritized improvement recommendations.\n   301â†’\n   302â†’**Quality score output** (SC-007):\n   303â†’```\n   304â†’{clarity: float, completeness: float, testability: float, consistency: float}\n   305â†’```\n   306â†’\n   307â†’Where each dimension is a float in the 0-10 range:\n   308â†’- `clarity` (0.0-10.0): Language precision, unambiguous requirements, clear behavioral definitions\n   309â†’- `completeness` (0.0-10.0): Coverage of essential elements, no missing requirements, all edge cases addressed\n   310â†’- `testability` (0.0-10.0): Measurable acceptance criteria, verifiable requirements, concrete test scenarios\n   311â†’- `consistency` (0.0-10.0): Internal coherence, no contradictions, aligned cross-references\n   312â†’\n   313â†’Each expert also produces prioritized improvement recommendations as new findings using the same structured schema from step 4a.\n   314â†’\n   315â†’#### Step 4d: Critique Incorporation and Scoring\n   316â†’\n   317â†’1. **Record quality scores**: Write all 4 quality dimension scores from step 4c into the spec frontmatter:\n   318â†’   ```yaml\n   319â†’   quality_scores:\n   320â†’     clarity: <float>\n   321â†’     completeness: <float>\n   322â†’     testability: <float>\n   323â†’     consistency: <float>\n   324â†’     overall: <float>\n   325â†’   ```\n   326â†’\n   327â†’2. **Compute overall score**: `overall = mean(clarity, completeness, testability, consistency)` â€” that is, `overall = (clarity + completeness + testability + consistency) / 4` (Constraint 6, SC-010).\n   328â†’\n   329â†’3. **Append panel report**: Generate `panel-report.md` in the working directory containing:\n   330â†’   - All focus findings from step 4a with incorporation status\n   331â†’   - All critique findings from step 4c with scores\n   332â†’   - Guard Condition Boundary Table (if produced)\n   333â†’   - Quality dimension scores and overall score\n   334â†’   - Convergence status\n   335â†’\n   336â†’#### Convergence Loop\n   337â†’\n   338â†’Steps 4a through 4d execute within a bounded convergence loop using state machine semantics.\n   339â†’\n   340â†’**States**:\n   341â†’- `REVIEWING` â€” Executing focus pass (4a) or critique pass (4c)\n   342â†’- `INCORPORATING` â€” Executing incorporation (4b or 4d)\n   343â†’- `SCORING` â€” Evaluating convergence after scoring (4d)\n   344â†’- `CONVERGED` â€” Terminal state: zero unaddressed CRITICALs, `status: success`\n   345â†’- `ESCALATED` â€” Terminal state: 3 iterations exhausted, `status: partial`\n   346â†’\n   347â†’**Transitions**:\n   348â†’```\n   349â†’REVIEWING â†’ INCORPORATING (findings produced)\n   350â†’INCORPORATING â†’ SCORING (incorporation complete, scores computed)\n   351â†’SCORING â†’ CONVERGED (zero unaddressed CRITICALs remaining)\n   352â†’SCORING â†’ REVIEWING (unaddressed CRITICALs remain, iteration < 3)\n   353â†’SCORING â†’ ESCALATED (unaddressed CRITICALs remain, iteration >= 3)\n   354â†’```\n   355â†’\n   356â†’**Iteration counter**: Initialize `iteration = 1` before first pass. Increment after each SCORING â†’ REVIEWING transition. Hard cap: `max_iterations = 3` (SC-008).\n   357â†’\n   358â†’**Convergence predicate**: After SCORING, check if any findings with `severity: CRITICAL` have status other than `[INCORPORATED]` or `[DISMISSED]`. If zero unaddressed CRITICALs â†’ transition to CONVERGED. Otherwise â†’ check iteration counter.\n   359â†’\n   360â†’**Terminal states**:\n   361â†’- **CONVERGED**: `status: success` â€” all CRITICALs addressed, spec is review-complete\n   362â†’- **ESCALATED**: `status: partial` â€” 3 iterations exhausted with unaddressed CRITICALs remaining. Escalate to user with: remaining CRITICAL findings, iteration history, and recommendation for manual resolution.\n   363â†’\n   364â†’#### Downstream Ready Gate\n   365â†’\n   366â†’After convergence loop terminates (either CONVERGED or ESCALATED):\n   367â†’\n   368â†’1. Evaluate `downstream_ready` gate: `if overall >= 7.0 then downstream_ready = true else downstream_ready = false` (Constraint 8, SC-012).\n   369â†’   - Boundary: `overall = 7.0` â†’ `downstream_ready: true`\n   370â†’   - Boundary: `overall = 6.9` â†’ `downstream_ready: false`\n   371â†’\n   372â†’2. **Timing**: Record `phase_4_end = current_time()`. Compute `phase_4_seconds = phase_4_end - phase_4_start`. Populate `phase_timing.phase_4_seconds` in the return contract (SC-013). If `phase_4_seconds > 900`, emit warning: \"Phase 4 exceeded 15-minute advisory target (NFR-002)\".\n   373â†’\n   374â†’3. Populate the return contract with:\n   375â†’   - `convergence_state`: `CONVERGED` or `ESCALATED`\n   376â†’   - `convergence_iterations`: number of iterations completed\n   377â†’   - `quality_scores`: all 4 dimensions + overall\n   378â†’   - `downstream_ready`: boolean\n   379â†’   - `phase_timing.phase_4_seconds`: elapsed seconds\n   380â†’\n   381â†’**Present final spec to user for approval before delivering.**\n   382â†’\n   383â†’## Decision Framework: What Becomes Programmatic\n   384â†’\n   385â†’The value of portification is moving orchestration out of inference. Here are concrete examples from tested workflows:\n   386â†’\n   387â†’| Operation | Classification | Why |\n   388â†’|-----------|---------------|-----|\n   389â†’| Enumerate repo files | Pure programmatic | `git ls-files` + pattern matching is deterministic |\n   390â†’| Classify file domains | Pure programmatic | Extension/path pattern rules, no judgment needed |\n   391â†’| Assign files to batches | Pure programmatic | Math: divide files by batch_size, assign to agents |\n   392â†’| Filter Pass 1 results for Pass 2 | Pure programmatic | Parse markdown, extract classifications, filter list |\n   393â†’| Analyze file for issues | Claude-assisted | Requires reading code, understanding context |\n   394â†’| Score variant quality | Hybrid | Formulas are programmatic, rubric evaluation is Claude |\n   395â†’| Validate structural integrity | Pure programmatic | Regex checks, section presence, field counts |\n   396â†’| Spot-check verification | Claude-assisted | Re-reads files, re-evaluates claims independently |\n   397â†’| Merge batch reports | Claude-assisted | Requires synthesis, deduplication, pattern extraction |\n   398â†’| Compute convergence score | Pure programmatic | `agreed / total` â€” arithmetic |\n   399â†’| Generate executive summary | Claude-assisted | Requires narrative synthesis |\n   400â†’\n   401â†’### Rule of Thumb\n   402â†’If you can write a Python function for it with clear inputâ†’output types and no ambiguity, make it programmatic. If it requires reading natural language, making judgments, or synthesizing information, use Claude with a gate to verify the output.\n   403â†’\n   404â†’## Pipeline Design Principles\n   405â†’\n   406â†’These inform Phase 2 pipeline specification and align with the unified-audit-gating architecture in `pipeline/`.\n   407â†’\n   408â†’### Critical Constraints\n   409â†’1. **Synchronous execution** â€” Sprint uses `threading` + `time.sleep()` polling. Use `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism. Do NOT use async/await.\n   410â†’2. **Gate function signatures** â€” All semantic checks return `tuple[bool, str]`. The reason string feeds diagnostics and retry decisions.\n   411â†’3. **Runner-authored truth** â€” Reports derive from runner-observed data (exit codes, artifacts, gates, monitor signals), not Claude's self-reported status.\n   412â†’4. **Deterministic flow control** â€” Python makes all decisions about what runs next. Claude never decides \"what's next\".\n   413â†’\n   414â†’### Shared Pipeline Patterns\n   415â†’5. **Reuse `pipeline/` primitives** â€” `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult`, `GateMode`, `GateCriteria`, `SemanticCheck`, `gate_passed()`, `ClaudeProcess`\n   416â†’6. **Gate modes** â€” `BLOCKING` (default) stops pipeline on failure. `TRAILING` defers evaluation. Use trailing only for quality checks that don't affect downstream data flow.\n   417â†’7. **Turn budget** â€” `TurnLedger` with debit/credit/guard for multi-subprocess pipelines. Pre-launch guards prevent launching when budget too low.\n   418â†’8. **Subprocess isolation** â€” 4-layer model: scoped work dir, git ceiling, isolated plugin dir, isolated settings dir.\n   419â†’9. **Context injection** â€” Prior results serialized into subsequent prompts. This works well for flexible, one-off tasks but breaks down for repeatable multi-step pipelines where you need:\n\n- **Deterministic control flow** â€” Python decides what runs when, not inference\n- **Formal artifact validation** â€” Gates check output quality programmatically\n- **Resume/retry** â€” Failed steps resume without re-running everything\n- **Live monitoring** â€” TUI shows progress, stall detection, diagnostics\n- **Budget economics** â€” Turn ledger tracks consumption across subprocesses\n- **Consistent behavior** â€” Same inputs produce structurally identical outputs every run\n\nThe existing `pipeline/` and `sprint/` modules already solve these problems. This skill bridges the gap by analyzing a workflow and generating a new CLI module that uses these proven patterns.\n\n## What Gets Generated\n\nA CLI subcommand package under `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`:\n\n| File | Purpose | When Generated |\n|------|---------|----------------|\n| `models.py` | Domain types extending `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult` | Always |\n| `gates.py` | `GateCriteria` + semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]` | Always |\n| `prompts.py` | LLM contract builders per Claude-assisted step | Always |\n| `config.py` | CLI arg resolution, file discovery, config construction | Always |\n| `executor.py` | Synchronous supervisor loop with `ThreadPoolExecutor` for parallelism | Always |\n| `monitor.py` | NDJSON incremental output parser with domain signals | Always |\n| `process.py` | `ClaudeProcess` subclass with domain-specific prompt building | Always |\n| `tui.py` | Rich live dashboard with gate state machine | Always |\n| `logging_.py` | Dual JSONL + Markdown execution logging | Always |\n| `diagnostics.py` | `DiagnosticCollector`, `FailureClassifier`, `ReportGenerator` | Always |\n| `commands.py` | Click CLI group and subcommands | Always |\n| `__init__.py` | Package exports | Always |\n| `inventory.py` | Pure-programmatic file discovery/classification | If workflow has discovery steps |\n| `filtering.py` | Pure-programmatic inter-step data filtering | If workflow has filtering between steps |\n\nThese file definitions inform the pipeline specification produced in Phase 2.\n\n## Required Input\n\n```\n/sc:cli-portify --workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>]\n```\n\n| Argument | Required | Description |\n|----------|----------|-------------|\n| `--workflow` | Yes | Skill directory path or `sc-*` name to portify |\n| `--name` | No | CLI subcommand name (default: derived from workflow) |\n| `--output` | No | Output directory (default: `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`) |\n| `--dry-run` | No | Show decomposition plan without generating spec |\n\n**STOP** if `--workflow` is not provided or the path doesn't resolve to a valid skill.\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\nFour phases, each producing artifacts that feed the next. Present output to user for review after Phases 1 and 2 before continuing.\n\n### Phase 1: Workflow Analysis\n\nLoad `refs/analysis-protocol.md` before this phase. It contains the discovery checklist, step decomposition algorithm, classification rubric, and output format template.\n\n**Goal**: Decompose the target workflow into a structured pipeline specification.\n\n1. **Discover components** â€” Find the command `.md`, skill `SKILL.md`, all `refs/` and `rules/`, all `templates/`, all `scripts/`, and all referenced agents. Build a component inventory table with paths, line counts, and purposes.\n\n2. **Map the protocol** â€” Extract the step-by-step behavioral flow. Pay attention to:\n   - Wave/phase boundaries in the skill\n   - Agent delegation patterns (which agent, parallel vs sequential)\n   - Conditional execution paths (flags that skip steps)\n   - Implicit inter-step data flow (what one step produces that another consumes)\n\n3. **Identify steps** â€” A new Step boundary exists when:\n   - A new artifact is produced\n   - A different agent takes over\n   - Execution mode changes (sequential â†’ parallel)\n   - A quality gate must be evaluated\n   - Operation type changes (analysis â†’ generation â†’ validation)\n\n4. **Classify each step** on the programmatic spectrum:\n   - **Pure programmatic**: Runs as a Python function, no Claude subprocess. Examples: file inventory via `git ls-files`, config construction, file filtering between passes, scoring formulas, structural validation, batch assignment. If the logic is deterministic and the input/output formats are well-defined, it should be programmatic.\n   - **Claude-assisted**: Runs as a Claude subprocess with a prompt contract and gate. Examples: content analysis, writing reports, rubric-based assessment, creative synthesis, debate.\n   - **Hybrid**: Programmatic setup â†’ Claude subprocess â†’ programmatic validation. Examples: steps that need Claude for content but have strict structural validation on the output.\n\n5. **Map dependencies and parallel groups** â€” Draw the data flow: which steps produce artifacts consumed by downstream steps? Which steps are independent and can run concurrently? For batched workflows, identify where batch parallelism applies.\n\n6. **Extract gates** â€” For each step output, identify what validation the original workflow expects. Map these to gate tiers: EXEMPT (informational), LIGHT (exists + non-empty), STANDARD (structural checks), STRICT (structural + semantic).\n\n7. **Assign gate modes** â€” `GateMode.BLOCKING` for steps whose output feeds downstream steps. `GateMode.TRAILING` for quality-only checks that don't affect data flow.\n\n**Output**: `portify-analysis.md` â€” Complete decomposition following the template in `refs/analysis-protocol.md`. Must include: component inventory, step graph with classifications, parallel groups, gates summary, data flow diagram, and recommendations.\n\n**Present to user for review before Phase 2.**\n\n### Phase 2: Pipeline Specification\n\nLoad `refs/pipeline-spec.md` before this phase. It contains Step definition patterns, model design patterns, gate patterns, executor patterns, and the new unified-audit-gating patterns (TurnLedger, gate modes, subprocess isolation, context injection, resume semantics).\n\n**Goal**: Convert the analysis into concrete, code-ready specifications.\n\n1. **Design the Step graph** â€” Map each workflow step to `Step` objects. Batched parallel steps are `list[Step]` groups. Dynamic step counts (e.g., batch count determined at runtime) require a `build_steps()` function.\n\n2. **Define models** â€” Design domain-specific dataclasses:\n   - Config extending `PipelineConfig` with workflow-specific fields (source paths, pass selection, batch sizes, stall/timeout policies)\n   - Status enum with domain-specific states (e.g., `VALIDATION_FAIL`, `CRITICAL_FAIL` for audit workflows)\n   - Result extending `StepResult` with execution telemetry\n   - Aggregate result with `resume_command()` and `suggested_resume_budget`\n   - Monitor state with domain-specific NDJSON signals\n   - `TurnLedger` integration for budget tracking\n\n3. **Design prompts** â€” For each Claude-assisted step, write the prompt builder. Each prompt must specify:\n   - What input files/context to embed (inline for <50KB, `--file` args for larger)\n   - Required output sections and frontmatter fields\n   - Machine-readable markers: `EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE|HALT`\n   - Any structural requirements the gate will check\n\n   If prompts collectively exceed ~300 lines, put them in a separate `portify-prompts.md`.\n\n4. **Design gates** â€” For each output artifact, define:\n   - `GateCriteria` with tier, required frontmatter, min lines, semantic checks\n   - `GateMode` (BLOCKING or TRAILING)\n   - All semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]`\n\n5. **Implement pure-programmatic steps** â€” Write actual runnable Python code for steps classified as \"pure programmatic\". These run as direct function calls in the executor, bypassing `ClaudeProcess`. Include: file discovery, domain classification, batch assignment, inter-pass filtering, config construction.\n\n6. **Design the executor** â€” Sprint-style synchronous supervisor:\n   - `ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism (NOT async/await)\n   - `time.sleep()` polling loops for monitoring\n   - Per-step/batch monitoring with stall detection\n   - `TurnLedger` budget guards before each launch\n   - Runner-authored truth: reports from observed data, not Claude self-reporting\n   - Subprocess isolation (4-layer model) for child Claude sessions\n   - Context injection: prior results compressed into subsequent prompts\n   - Signal-aware shutdown with `SignalHandler`\n\n7. **Plan integration** â€” Click command group, main.py import, file generation order.\n\n**Output**: `portify-spec.md` (+ optional `portify-prompts.md`) â€” Complete code spec with models, gates, executor design, pure-programmatic implementations, and integration plan.\n\n**Present to user for approval before Phase 3.**\n\n### Phase 3: Release Spec Synthesis\n\n**Phase 2â†’3 Entry Gate**: Before beginning Phase 3, verify ALL of the following:\n- Phase 2 contract `status: completed`\n- All blocking checks passed (no unresolved BLOCKING gate failures)\n- Phase 2 `step_mapping` contains â‰Ą1 entry\n\n**STOP** if any entry gate condition fails. Report which condition failed and emit the return contract with `failure_phase: 3, failure_type: prerequisite_failed`.\n\n**Goal**: Generate a complete, reviewed release specification from Phase 1 and Phase 2 outputs. Record the wall clock start time for `phase_3_seconds` timing instrumentation.\n\n**Timing**: Record `phase_3_start = current_time()` at the beginning of this phase. NFR-001 advisory target: Phase 3 should complete within 10 minutes wall clock (non-blocking; exceeding this target emits a warning but does not halt the pipeline).\n\n#### Step 3a: Template Instantiation\n\n1. Load the release spec template from `src/superclaude/examples/release-spec-template.md`\n2. Create a working copy at `{work_dir}/portify-release-spec.md`\n3. Verify the working copy was created successfully and contains the template content\n\n#### Step 3b: Content Population\n\nFill template sections from Phase 1 (workflow analysis) and Phase 2 (pipeline specification) outputs using the following mapping table. For each template section, replace `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` sentinels with content derived from the specified source:\n\n| # | Template Section | Source |\n|---|-----------------|--------|\n| 1 | Problem Statement | Derive from source workflow's purpose + why portification is needed |\n| 2 | Solution Overview | Phase 2 pipeline architecture (step graph, executor design) |\n| 2.2 | Workflow / Data Flow | Phase 1 data flow diagram, adapted for the target pipeline |\n| 3 | Functional Requirements | One FR per generated pipeline step from Phase 2 `step_mapping` â€” every `step_mapping` entry MUST produce a corresponding FR (SC-004) |\n| 4 | Architecture | Phase 2 `module_plan` (new files), Phase 0 prerequisites (modified files) |\n| 4.5 | Data Models | Phase 2 model designs (Config, Status, Result, MonitorState) |\n| 4.6 | Implementation Order | Phase 2 module dependency order |\n| 5.2 | Gate Criteria | Phase 2 `gate_definitions` |\n| 5.3 | Phase Contracts | Phase 1+2 contract schemas |\n| 6 | NFRs | Standard portification NFRs (sync execution, gate signatures, runner-authored truth) |\n| 7 | Risk Assessment | Derived from Phase 1 classification confidence scores + unsupported patterns |\n| 8 | Test Plan | Structural test plan from Phase 2 pattern coverage matrix |\n| 10 | Downstream Inputs | Themes for sc:roadmap, tasks for sc:tasklist |\n\nAfter populating all sections, run SC-003 self-validation: verify zero remaining `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` sentinels in the working copy. If any remain, resolve them before proceeding.\n\n#### Step 3c: Automated Brainstorm Pass\n\nApply embedded brainstorm behavioral patterns as a non-interactive automated pass against the draft spec. This is NOT an invocation of the `sc:brainstorm` command (which is interactive/Socratic); instead, cycle through each of three personas to analyze the draft spec for gaps:\n\n**Persona perspectives** (apply each in sequence):\n\n1. **Architect persona**: Analyze for structural gaps â€” missing dependencies, incomplete module boundaries, scaling concerns, cross-module interaction gaps, missing error handling paths\n2. **Analyzer persona**: Analyze for logical gaps â€” uncovered edge cases, ambiguous requirements, missing acceptance criteria, inconsistent cross-references, untestable requirements\n3. **Backend persona**: Analyze for implementation gaps â€” missing data models, incomplete API contracts, undefined error states, missing retry/timeout specifications, resource lifecycle gaps\n\n**Structured output format**: Each finding uses the schema:\n```\n{gap_id, description, severity(high|medium|low), affected_section, persona}\n```\n\nExample:\n```\n{GAP-001, \"No retry policy defined for failed gate checks\", medium, \"5.2 Gate Criteria\", architect}\n```\n\n**Zero-gap handling**: If no gaps are identified across all three personas, produce an explicit summary:\n> \"No gaps identified by architect, analyzer, and backend personas. Spec coverage assessed as complete.\"\n\nSet `gaps_identified: 0` in the return contract. Zero gaps is a valid outcome â€” it does not block the pipeline.\n\n**Output**: Append a `## Brainstorm Gap Analysis` section (Section 12) to the draft spec containing all findings in the structured format, or the zero-gap summary.\n\n#### Step 3d: Gap Incorporation\n\nReview each brainstorm finding and route it:\n\n- **Actionable findings** (findings that can be directly addressed): Incorporate into the relevant spec body section identified by `affected_section`. Mark the finding as `[INCORPORATED]` in the gap analysis table.\n- **Unresolvable items** (findings that require external input, are out of scope, or cannot be resolved within the spec): Route to Section 11 (Open Items) with the gap ID, question, impact, and resolution target. Mark the finding as `[OPEN]` in the gap analysis table.\n\nAfter incorporation, update the gap analysis summary with counts: `{total_gaps, incorporated, open, severity_distribution}`.\n\n**Timing**: Record `phase_3_end = current_time()`. Compute `phase_3_seconds = phase_3_end - phase_3_start`. Populate `phase_timing.phase_3_seconds` in the return contract. If `phase_3_seconds > 600`, emit warning: \"Phase 3 exceeded 10-minute advisory target (NFR-001)\".\n\n**Output**: `{work_dir}/portify-release-spec.md` â€” Complete draft spec with brainstorm gap analysis section and incorporated findings.\n\n**Phase 3â†’4 automatic gate**: Draft spec populated (no `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` values remain) AND brainstorm section (Section 12) present in draft spec.\n\n### Phase 4: Spec Panel Review\n\nEmbed `sc:spec-panel` behavioral patterns in a convergent review loop. Like Phase 3's brainstorm, this embeds spec-panel behavioral patterns directly rather than invoking the `sc:spec-panel` command (Constraint 1: no inter-skill command invocation).\n\n**Timing**: Record `phase_4_start = current_time()` at the beginning of this phase. NFR-002 advisory target: Phase 4 should complete within 15 minutes wall clock (non-blocking; exceeding this target emits a warning but does not halt the pipeline).\n\n#### Step 4a: Focus Pass\n\nApply spec-panel behavioral patterns with `--focus correctness,architecture` against `portify-release-spec.md`. This pass embeds four expert analysis patterns inline:\n\n**Expert analysis patterns** (apply each in sequence, building on prior context):\n\n1. **Fowler (Architecture)**: Analyze interface design quality, bounded context boundaries, module coupling/cohesion, dependency direction, and design pattern appropriateness. Annotate data flows with count divergence analysis â€” for each transformation, document input count, output count, and whether the spec accounts for count differences.\n\n2. **Nygard (Reliability/Failure Modes)**: Analyze failure mode coverage, circuit breaker patterns, timeout specifications, retry policies, and recovery mechanisms. Extend guard boundary analysis to include zero/empty cases â€” for every guard condition, verify the spec defines behavior for zero, empty, null, and negative inputs.\n\n3. **Whittaker (Adversarial)**: Apply five attack methodologies (Zero/Empty, Divergence, Sentinel Collision, Sequence, Accumulation) against each identified invariant. Produce concrete attack scenarios with state traces demonstrating specification gaps.\n\n4. **Crispin (Testing)**: Analyze testing strategy coverage, acceptance criteria quality, edge case identification, and quality attribute specifications. Generate boundary value test cases for every guard condition and state variable covering: below minimum, at minimum, typical, at maximum, above maximum, and degenerate (zero/empty/null).\n\n**Focus dimensions**: `correctness` and `architecture` â€” findings must address both dimensions (SC-006).\n\n**Output format**: Each finding uses the structured schema:\n```\n{finding_id, severity(CRITICAL|MAJOR|MINOR), expert, location, issue, recommendation}\n```\n\nWhere:\n- `finding_id`: Unique identifier (e.g., `F-001`, `F-002`)\n- `severity`: One of `CRITICAL` (spec provably wrong), `MAJOR` (spec ambiguous/incomplete), `MINOR` (spec could be clearer)\n- `expert`: One of `Fowler`, `Nygard`, `Whittaker`, `Crispin`\n- `location`: Section/requirement reference in the spec\n- `issue`: Description of the identified problem\n- `recommendation`: Specific actionable fix\n\nAdditionally produce, if applicable:\n- Guard Condition Boundary Table (Nygard leads, Crispin validates, Whittaker attacks)\n- Pipeline Quantity Flow Diagram (Fowler leads, if pipeline stages detected)\n- State Variable Registry (if 3+ mutable state variables identified)\n\n#### Step 4b: Focus Incorporation\n\nReview focus findings from step 4a. Route each finding by severity level. All modifications MUST be additive-only â€” append or extend spec sections only, do not rewrite existing content (Constraint 2, NFR-008).\n\n**Severity routing**:\n\n- **CRITICAL findings**: MUST be addressed. Either:\n  - Incorporate the fix into the relevant spec body section identified by `location`, OR\n  - Document a written justification for dismissal in the panel report (Constraint 7). Dismissal justification must include: `finding_id`, reason for dismissal, and assessment of downstream impact.\n- **MAJOR findings**: Incorporate into the corresponding spec body section identified by `location`. Modifications use append/extend only.\n- **MINOR findings**: Append to Section 11 (Open Items) with the `finding_id`, issue summary, and recommended resolution target.\n\nAll modifications are traceable by `finding_id` from step 4a output. Mark each finding as `[INCORPORATED]`, `[DISMISSED]`, or `[OPEN]` in the focus findings table.\n\n#### Step 4c: Critique Pass\n\nApply spec-panel behavioral patterns with `--mode critique` against the updated spec (after step 4b incorporation). Run the full expert panel in critique review sequence:\n\n1. Fowler â€” Architecture and interface design\n2. Nygard â€” Reliability and failure mode analysis\n3. Whittaker â€” Adversarial attack-based specification probing\n4. Crispin â€” Testing strategy and acceptance criteria\n\nEach expert produces quality dimension scores and prioritized improvement recommendations.\n\n**Quality score output** (SC-007):\n```\n{clarity: float, completeness: float, testability: float, consistency: float}\n```\n\nWhere each dimension is a float in the 0-10 range:\n- `clarity` (0.0-10.0): Language precision, unambiguous requirements, clear behavioral definitions\n- `completeness` (0.0-10.0): Coverage of essential elements, no missing requirements, all edge cases addressed\n- `testability` (0.0-10.0): Measurable acceptance criteria, verifiable requirements, concrete test scenarios\n- `consistency` (0.0-10.0): Internal coherence, no contradictions, aligned cross-references\n\nEach expert also produces prioritized improvement recommendations as new findings using the same structured schema from step 4a.\n\n#### Step 4d: Critique Incorporation and Scoring\n\n1. **Record quality scores**: Write all 4 quality dimension scores from step 4c into the spec frontmatter:\n   ```yaml\n   quality_scores:\n     clarity: <float>\n     completeness: <float>\n     testability: <float>\n     consistency: <float>\n     overall: <float>\n   ```\n\n2. **Compute overall score**: `overall = mean(clarity, completeness, testability, consistency)` â€” that is, `overall = (clarity + completeness + testability + consistency) / 4` (Constraint 6, SC-010).\n\n3. **Append panel report**: Generate `panel-report.md` in the working directory containing:\n   - All focus findings from step 4a with incorporation status\n   - All critique findings from step 4c with scores\n   - Guard Condition Boundary Table (if produced)\n   - Quality dimension scores and overall score\n   - Convergence status\n\n#### Convergence Loop\n\nSteps 4a through 4d execute within a bounded convergence loop using state machine semantics.\n\n**States**:\n- `REVIEWING` â€” Executing focus pass (4a) or critique pass (4c)\n- `INCORPORATING` â€” Executing incorporation (4b or 4d)\n- `SCORING` â€” Evaluating convergence after scoring (4d)\n- `CONVERGED` â€” Terminal state: zero unaddressed CRITICALs, `status: success`\n- `ESCALATED` â€” Terminal state: 3 iterations exhausted, `status: partial`\n\n**Transitions**:\n```\nREVIEWING â†’ INCORPORATING (findings produced)\nINCORPORATING â†’ SCORING (incorporation complete, scores computed)\nSCORING â†’ CONVERGED (zero unaddressed CRITICALs remaining)\nSCORING â†’ REVIEWING (unaddressed CRITICALs remain, iteration < 3)\nSCORING â†’ ESCALATED (unaddressed CRITICALs remain, iteration >= 3)\n```\n\n**Iteration counter**: Initialize `iteration = 1` before first pass. Increment after each SCORING â†’ REVIEWING transition. Hard cap: `max_iterations = 3` (SC-008).\n\n**Convergence predicate**: After SCORING, check if any findings with `severity: CRITICAL` have status other than `[INCORPORATED]` or `[DISMISSED]`. If zero unaddressed CRITICALs â†’ transition to CONVERGED. Otherwise â†’ check iteration counter.\n\n**Terminal states**:\n- **CONVERGED**: `status: success` â€” all CRITICALs addressed, spec is review-complete\n- **ESCALATED**: `status: partial` â€” 3 iterations exhausted with unaddressed CRITICALs remaining. Escalate to user with: remaining CRITICAL findings, iteration history, and recommendation for manual resolution.\n\n#### Downstream Ready Gate\n\nAfter convergence loop terminates (either CONVERGED or ESCALATED):\n\n1. Evaluate `downstream_ready` gate: `if overall >= 7.0 then downstream_ready = true else downstream_ready = false` (Constraint 8, SC-012).\n   - Boundary: `overall = 7.0` â†’ `downstream_ready: true`\n   - Boundary: `overall = 6.9` â†’ `downstream_ready: false`\n\n2. **Timing**: Record `phase_4_end = current_time()`. Compute `phase_4_seconds = phase_4_end - phase_4_start`. Populate `phase_timing.phase_4_seconds` in the return contract (SC-013). If `phase_4_seconds > 900`, emit warning: \"Phase 4 exceeded 15-minute advisory target (NFR-002)\".\n\n3. Populate the return contract with:\n   - `convergence_state`: `CONVERGED` or `ESCALATED`\n   - `convergence_iterations`: number of iterations completed\n   - `quality_scores`: all 4 dimensions + overall\n   - `downstream_ready`: boolean\n   - `phase_timing.phase_4_seconds`: elapsed seconds\n\n**Present final spec to user for approval before delivering.**\n\n## Decision Framework: What Becomes Programmatic\n\nThe value of portification is moving orchestration out of inference. Here are concrete examples from tested workflows:\n\n| Operation | Classification | Why |\n|-----------|---------------|-----|\n| Enumerate repo files | Pure programmatic | `git ls-files` + pattern matching is deterministic |\n| Classify file domains | Pure programmatic | Extension/path pattern rules, no judgment needed |\n| Assign files to batches | Pure programmatic | Math: divide files by batch_size, assign to agents |\n| Filter Pass 1 results for Pass 2 | Pure programmatic | Parse markdown, extract classifications, filter list |\n| Analyze file for issues | Claude-assisted | Requires reading code, understanding context |\n| Score variant quality | Hybrid | Formulas are programmatic, rubric evaluation is Claude |\n| Validate structural integrity | Pure programmatic | Regex checks, section presence, field counts |\n| Spot-check verification | Claude-assisted | Re-reads files, re-evaluates claims independently |\n| Merge batch reports | Claude-assisted | Requires synthesis, deduplication, pattern extraction |\n| Compute convergence score | Pure programmatic | `agreed / total` â€” arithmetic |\n| Generate executive summary | Claude-assisted | Requires narrative synthesis |\n\n### Rule of Thumb\nIf you can write a Python function for it with clear inputâ†’output types and no ambiguity, make it programmatic. If it requires reading natural language, making judgments, or synthesizing information, use Claude with a gate to verify the output.\n\n## Pipeline Design Principles\n\nThese inform Phase 2 pipeline specification and align with the unified-audit-gating architecture in `pipeline/`.\n\n### Critical Constraints\n1. **Synchronous execution** â€” Sprint uses `threading` + `time.sleep()` polling. Use `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism. Do NOT use async/await.\n2. **Gate function signatures** â€” All semantic checks return `tuple[bool, str]`. The reason string feeds diagnostics and retry decisions.\n3. **Runner-authored truth** â€” Reports derive from runner-observed data (exit codes, artifacts, gates, monitor signals), not Claude's self-reported status.\n4. **Deterministic flow control** â€” Python makes all decisions about what runs next. Claude never decides \"what's next\".\n\n### Shared Pipeline Patterns\n5. **Reuse `pipeline/` primitives** â€” `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult`, `GateMode`, `GateCriteria`, `SemanticCheck`, `gate_passed()`, `ClaudeProcess`\n6. **Gate modes** â€” `BLOCKING` (default) stops pipeline on failure. `TRAILING` defers evaluation. Use trailing only for quality checks that don't affect downstream data flow.\n7. **Turn budget** â€” `TurnLedger` with debit/credit/guard for multi-subprocess pipelines. Pre-launch guards prevent launching when budget too low.\n8. **Subprocess isolation** â€” 4-layer model: scoped work dir, git ceiling, isolated plugin dir, isolated settings dir.\n9. **Context injection** â€” Prior results serialized into subsequent prompts. Compress older, preserve recent.\n10. **Resume-first failures** â€” On halt: exact resume command, remaining work, diagnostic path, budget suggestion.\n11. **Diagnostic chain** â€” Runner-side failure analysis that doesn't consume turn budget.\n\n### Output Guidance\n- `portify-analysis.md`: Under 400 lines. Step graph, gates, data flow.\n- `portify-spec.md`: Split prompts to separate file if spec exceeds 800 lines.\n- Pure-programmatic steps: Full implementation code, not descriptions.\n\n## Boundaries\n\n### Will Do\n- Analyze any SuperClaude skill/command/agent workflow\n- Decompose into structured pipeline specification\n- Generate a complete release specification via template instantiation and brainstorm pass\n- Run spec panel review for quality validation\n- Produce a downstream-ready spec for sc:roadmap and sc:tasklist\n\n### Will Not Do\n- Generate code files directly (use the release spec with sc:implement instead)\n- Execute the generated pipeline\n- Modify original skill/command/agent files\n- Create new skills or agents\n- Make architectural decisions about the workflow's logic\n\n## Return Contract Schema\n\nThe return contract is emitted on **every invocation** including success, partial completion, failure, and dry-run (SC-009). All fields are always present; default values apply on failure paths.\n\n### Contract Fields\n\n```yaml\n# --- Identity ---\ncontract_version: \"2.0\"            # Schema version for downstream compatibility\nspec_file: \"<path>\"                 # Path to generated release spec (empty string on failure)\npanel_report: \"<path>\"              # Path to panel-report.md (empty string if not produced)\noutput_directory: \"<path>\"          # Working directory for all artifacts\n\n# --- Quality Scores (SC-007, SC-010) ---\nquality_scores:\n  clarity: <float>                  # 0.0-10.0 â€” Language precision, unambiguous requirements\n  completeness: <float>             # 0.0-10.0 â€” Coverage of essential elements\n  testability: <float>              # 0.0-10.0 â€” Measurable acceptance criteria\n  consistency: <float>              # 0.0-10.0 â€” Internal coherence, no contradictions\n  overall: <float>                  # mean(clarity, completeness, testability, consistency) (SC-010)\n\n# --- Convergence ---\nconvergence_iterations: <int>       # Number of review loop iterations completed (0 on failure)\nconvergence_state: \"<state>\"        # CONVERGED | ESCALATED | NOT_STARTED\n\n# --- Timing (SC-013) ---\nphase_timing:\n  phase_3_seconds: <float>          # Wall clock seconds for Phase 3 (0.0 if not reached)\n  phase_4_seconds: <float>          # Wall clock seconds for Phase 4 (0.0 if not reached)\n\n# --- Pipeline Metadata ---\nsource_step_count: <int>            # Number of steps identified in Phase 1 analysis\nspec_fr_count: <int>                # Number of functional requirements in generated spec\napi_snapshot_hash: \"<hash>\"         # SHA-256 of the pipeline-spec.md at time of spec generation\n\n# --- Downstream Readiness (SC-012) Contracts ---\nphase_contracts:\n  phase_0: \"<status>\"               # completed | skipped | failed\n  phase_1: \"<status>\"               # completed | skipped | failed\n  phase_2: \"<status>\"               # completed | skipped | failed\n  phase_3: \"<status>\"               # completed | skipped | failed\n  phase_4: \"<status>\"               # completed | skipped | failed\n\n# --- Warnings ---\nwarnings: []                        # List of advisory messages (e.g., timing threshold exceeded)\n\n# --- Failure Information ---\nstatus: \"<status>\"                  # success | partial | failed | dry_run\nfailure_phase: <int|null>           # Phase number where failure occurred (null on success)\nfailure_type: \"<type|null>\"         # Failure type enumeration value (null on success)\n\n# --- Resume Support ---\nresume_phase: <int|null>            # Phase to resume from (null if not resumable)\nresume_substep: \"<substep|null>\"    # Substep within phase to resume from (null if not resumable)\nresume_command: \"<command|null>\"    # Full CLI command to resume execution (null if not resumable)\n```\n\n### Failure Type Enumeration\n\nThe `failure_type` field uses the following enumeration to classify failures:\n\n| Value | Description | Resumable | Resume Point |\n|-------|-------------|-----------|--------------|\n| `template_failed` | Release spec template could not be loaded or instantiated | No | â€” |\n| `brainstorm_failed` | Automated brainstorm pass failed to produce findings | Yes | `3c` |\n| `brainstorm_timeout` | Brainstorm pass exceeded time budget | Yes | `3c` |\n| `focus_failed` | Spec panel focus pass failed to produce findings | Yes | `4a` |\n| `critique_failed` | Spec panel critique pass failed to produce scores | Yes | `4a` |\n| `convergence_exhausted` | Maximum convergence iterations (3) reached with unresolved CRITICALs | No | â€” |\n| `user_rejected` | User rejected spec at an approval gate | No | â€” |\n| `prerequisite_failed` | Phase entry gate condition not met | No | â€” |\n\n### Failure Path Defaults (NFR-009)\n\nOn any failure path, the contract is emitted with these defaults:\n- All `quality_scores` fields default to `0.0` (NOT null)\n- `downstream_ready` defaults to `false`\n- `convergence_iterations` defaults to `0`\n- `convergence_state` defaults to `NOT_STARTED`\n- `spec_file` and `panel_report` default to `\"\"` (empty string)\n- `resume_substep` is populated for resumable failure types; null otherwise\n- All `phase_contracts` entries for incomplete phases default to `failed`\n- `phase_timing` entries default to `0.0` for phases not reached\n\n### Resume Behavior Semantics\n\n**Phase 3 Resume** (`resume_substep=3c`):\n- Preserves the populated spec from Step 3b (template instantiation + content population)\n- Brainstorm pass (Step 3c) re-runs from scratch against the preserved draft\n- Gap incorporation (Step 3d) re-runs after brainstorm completes\n- All Phase 1 and Phase 2 artifacts are preserved unchanged\n\n**Phase 4 Resume** (`resume_substep=4a`):\n- Preserves the complete draft spec from Phase 3 (including brainstorm findings)\n- Focus pass (Step 4a) re-runs from scratch against the preserved spec\n- All subsequent steps (4b, 4c, 4d) re-run in sequence\n- Convergence loop resets iteration counter to 1\n- All Phase 1, Phase 2, and Phase 3 artifacts are preserved unchanged\n\n### Contract Emission on Dry Run\n\nWhen `--dry-run` is active, the contract is emitted with:\n- `status: dry_run`\n- Phases 0-2 contracts populated; Phases 3-4 marked as `skipped`\n- All quality scores set to `0.0`\n- `downstream_ready: false`\n- `convergence_state: NOT_STARTED`\n- No spec synthesis or panel review artifacts produced\n\n## Related Commands\n\n- `/sc:implement` â€” General feature implementation\n- `/sc:design` â€” System architecture design\n- `/sc:analyze` â€” Code analysis for understanding workflows\n- `/sc:build` â€” Build \"1.0.0\"\n---\n\n# /sc:cli-portify\n\nConvert inference-based SuperClaude workflows (commands + skills + agents) into programmatic CLI pipelines with deterministic control flow, formal artifact validation, and live monitoring.\n\n## Triggers\n\nWhen the user requests workflow portification, CLI pipeline conversion, or programmatic workflow generation from an existing skill.\n\n## Usage\n\n```\n/sc:cli-portify --workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>] [--dry-run] [--skip-integration]\n```\n\nBoth `@file` syntax and explicit file paths are supported for `--workflow`.\n\n## Arguments\n\n| Argument | Required | Default | Description |\n|----------|----------|---------|-------------|\n| `--workflow` | Yes | -- | Skill directory path or `sc-*` name to portify. |\n| `--name` | No | Derived from workflow name | CLI subcommand name (kebab-case). |\n| `--output` | No | `src/superclaude/cli/<derived-name>/` | Output directory for the generated CLI module. |\n| `--dry-run` | No | false | Execute Phases 0-2 only â€” emit Phase 0-2 contracts only. No spec synthesis (Phase 3) or panel review (Phase 4) artifacts are produced. |\n| `--skip-integration` | No | false | Generate module only, skip main.py wiring (Phase 4). |\n\n### Name Derivation\n\nWhen `--name` is not provided, derive from the workflow:\n1. Strip `sc-` prefix if present\n2. Strip `-protocol` suffix if present\n3. Convert to kebab-case for CLI, snake_case for Python modules\n\n## Input Validation\n\nBefore invoking the skill, validate all inputs. On any validation failure, emit an error and exit without invoking the skill.\n\n**Error format:**\n```\nerror_code: <ERROR_CODE>\nmessage: <human-readable description with corrective action>\n```\n\n**Validation checks:**\n\n1. **Workflow argument present**: `--workflow` must be provided.\n   - Error: `error_code: MISSING_WORKFLOW` / `message: \"--workflow is required. Provide a skill directory path or sc-* name.\"`\n\n2. **Workflow path resolves**: The workflow path resolves to a directory containing `SKILL.md`.\n   - Error: `error_code: INVALID_PATH` / `message: \"Path '<path>' does not exist or does not contain a SKILL.md file.\"`\n\n3. **Workflow path unambiguous**: Only one candidate directory matches the workflow name.\n   - Error: `error_code: AMBIGUOUS_PATH` / `message: \"Multiple candidates found for '<name>': <list>. Use a full path to disambiguate.\"`\n\n4. **Output directory writable**: If `--output` is provided, its parent directory exists and is writable.\n   - Error: `error_code: OUTPUT_NOT_WRITABLE` / `message: \"Output directory parent '<parent>' does not exist or is not writable.\"`\n\n5. **No name collision**: The derived or provided `--name` does not collide with an existing non-portified CLI module.\n   - Error: `error_code: NAME_COLLISION` / `message: \"CLI module '<name>' already exists at '<path>' and was not generated by portification. Use --name to specify an alternative.\"`\n\n6. **Name derivation succeeds**: If `--name` is not provided, derivation from the workflow name produces a valid identifier.\n   - Error: `error_code: DERIVATION_FAILED` / `message: \"Could not derive CLI name from workflow '<name>'. Use --name to specify explicitly.\"`\n\n## Activation\n\n**Classification**: STRICT -- multi-file code generation operation with API conformance requirements.\n\n**MANDATORY**: Before executing any protocol steps, invoke:\n> Skill sc:cli-portify-protocol\n\nPass the following context:\n- Workflow path: resolved path to the skill directory\n- CLI name: resolved name (derived or from --name)\n- Output directory: resolved output path\n- Dry run: boolean flag value\n- Skip integration: boolean flag value\n\nDo NOT attempt to execute portification using only this command file.\nThe full portification protocol is in the protocol skill.\n\n## Examples\n\n```bash\n# Basic: portify a skill\n/sc:cli-portify --workflow src/superclaude/skills/sc-cleanup-audit/\n\n# With explicit name\n/sc:cli-portify --workflow sc-cleanup-audit --name cleanup-audit\n\n# Dry run (analysis only, no code generation)\n/sc:cli-portify --workflow sc-adversarial --dry-run\n\n# Skip main.py integration\n/sc:cli-portify --workflow sc-roadmap --skip-integration\n\n# Full invocation\n/sc:cli-portify --workflow src/superclaude/skills/sc-tasklist-protocol/ --name tasklist --output src/superclaude/cli/tasklist/\n```\n\n## Boundaries\n\n**Will:**\n- Parse and validate input arguments\n- Derive CLI name from workflow name\n- Resolve workflow path to a skill directory\n- Invoke the protocol skill with validated context\n- Report generated file paths on completion\n\n**Will Not:**\n- Execute the portification protocol (that is the skill's job)\n- Modify source skill files\n- Run the generated CLI pipeline\n- Generate anything beyond what the protocol produces\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":20,"oldLines":7,"newStart":20,"newLines":7,"lines":[" ##
